<Review>Great service and prices! Way better than the large national chains like discount/America's tire. I purchased a set of tires from Pacific Tires about 16 years ago, but since I don't live in LA, I had not been here since. I was visiting from out of town (Utah) and needed a new set of tires before my 650+ mile drive home. Came here on a Sunday morning, both because they were one of the only local tire shops that was open, and because I had a good previous experience. I arrived as soon as the shop opened and was assisted immediately. The shop manager was super helpful, not pushy at all. The price offered was straight forward and included all charges out the door. This was a breathe of fresh air as my experience with the national chains (Discount Tire) is the opposite. They installed my tires right away. I was in and out in under 45 min. I will come back in the future.< /Review>< rate>

This place was amazing! Needed two front tires, had a nail in my back rear tire and needed a spare is what I was told when I got my oil changed earlier today at another place! Went to Pacific off of a recommendation from a coworker and they said the same thing. Fernando helped me and his customer service was nothing less than amazing! He checked the one with the nail and the nail was small when he pulled it out & after inspecting it said it was fine and didn't need to replace it! He recommended two Used front tires that were matching and in amazing condition! 2 for $100! He also let me keep one of my front tires to use as a spare, which was amazing considering my spare was in terrible, Non drive-able condition. Overall spent $110! Not only top notch, HONEST service but such quick service (in and out in 30min) AND OPEN ON A SUNDAY!! I'll definitely be going back here for any services I might need! Thank you Pacific and thank you Fernando!!< /text>

<Pics>None< /Pics><Rate>5<//Rate><gmapID>0x808e4044b5d0d5d1:0xe861b93b14e964b6<//gmapID><Time>1572390491659< /Time><Text>My wife and I ate here. The food is excellent. Service also. We will be back if we are in the area again.</Text></record></dataset><record>
<gmapID>0x808e4044b5d0d5d1:0xe861b93b14e964b6< /gmapID><pictures>None</pictures>< Text>
My wife and I and another couple went here because we were able to get reservations just a couple days earlier.  Being Valentine's Day, we expected it to be busy.  What we didn't expect was to be seated in a seldom used back room with virtually zero ambiance.  To get there, we were led past an area being set up for what looked to be a wedding the next day.  There was a large flat screen display with what appeared to be a screen saver application displaying the name of a music station that was playing in the background.

The waitress did a great job of trying to make up for the stark setting with very cherry service but all her efforts couldn't overcome the poor quality in preparation of the food coming out of the kitchen.  Three of our party ordered the NY Steak.  These were served with garlic mashed potatoes and what was described on the menu as roasted asparagus.  The asparagus was boiled and all items on the plate were luke warm.  The first request to have the food heated to a more appealing temperature was met by the plates coming back with the ceramic hot but the food still only warm.  We gave up on getting everything hot and asked for a side of the potatoes HOT.  That worked and got those three thru the meal.  My wife complained that the steak seemed to have been freezer burned in that though it was indeed pink in the middle, it had a chalky texture and was dry.

The good news was that my salmon was perfectly done, making up partially for the luke warm fingerling potatoes.  The mixed vegetables were seasoned nicely though also luke warm.

We finished off with the berry cobbler and that was ok, but a bit on the sweet side.

They really need to figure out how to handle a larger than normal crowd or stick to their bar food gig that they actually do quite well.</Text>

<response>{'time': 1597874881644, 'text': 'Brian, Thanks for writing Your experience in detail ;)'}< /response><Time>1597293168476< /Time><user_id>101876271661184473784</user_id><text>As a Los Angeles native, I hold a record experience of having tried the best of the best cuisines, that exist in this city. Some search for the food, some search for the music, some search for the aesthetics, and although these are merely in part, it is very rare that I would find something that resonates with my very soul. Something that is not in part, but in full.

This, is that place.

For the first time in my life, I have found something that holds the key of being intentional, led with discretion and privacy, held together by the beauty of establishment in kindness and consideration.

2. SETTING
Kappo Osen is like a person's soul. It holds different rooms for a different purpose. There are dog-friendly patio sections where you still feel the breeze of the nearby ocean while at the same time having blankets and heaters ready to balance the atmosphere. There are areas where it is more private and you can even take off your shoes and wear their special sandals they provide (of which each are new and you can even take home!) and you can reserve ahead of time. There are also bar areas and areas where you can sit down in front of the chefs. All are open to the public, it just depends on what type of experience you are looking for. The outer decor is more surrounded by images but the interior decor has multiple touches of beauty, from a samurai armor piece to the private at-home feeling with a bar section fit to welcome a lively party group. The music is fit for each occasion depending on the time of day, but I love how the volume isn't so loud; It allows for you to be present with other people while at the same time not being completely silent among conversation.

3. PRICE, QUANTITY, & QUALITY FOR PRICE
$50+ per person (Includes tip)

Depending on what you order, it can vary. If you don't eat much, with tip, it would probably be a minimum of $40, but if you truly want an overall experience, it will most likely result in about $80+ per person ($80 already includes tip). They do offer certain alcoholic drinks and items that can range in the $$$ range, it just depends on what the occasion is and what you're looking for. Don't let the portions of the food fool you. It may seem not as big but it is very filling; Think of many small dishes, multiple flavors with a very satisfying experience.

Reservations
Even though walk-ins are available, it is highly recommended that you make a reservation ahead of time, always. It can get VERY busy here, with a wait time of 40 minutes to 2 hours. It is noted that many people will be willing to wait because they know it's worth it, so again, make reservations.
If you have a party of about 10 - 12 people, you can reserve it ahead of time, given that you make a down payment, so as to make everything run smoothly. I love this area in particular because it has closing blinds for privacy; It gives the experience, a taste of Japan.

D. It is HIGHLY suggested to save room for dessert. Their dessert menu is limited but elite in overall experience, as I found this part of the course, most exciting and the most memorable. I ordered the matcha cake with green tea ice cream. It was PERFECT. 5/5. 10/10/ 100/100

5. FINAL THOUGHTS
Kappo Osen is a wonderful place for being present; Whether it be for a special date, business, a group of friends, or catching up with a friend after a long time of not seeing them. It represents aesthetic intentionality, privacy, and creates an atmosphere where you can be fully present. This is, my very heart, a finished portrait and the fullness thereof.< /text><user_name>Brian Vasquez< /user_name></record>

Your experience at Kappo Osen will much depend on how and what you order. If not careful, you may order well over and eat $100 in food per person, and are likely to not perceive value relative to a $300-400 bill for two. On the other hand, you can also spend less than $100 after alcohol, taxes and tips, and be happy with the outcome. I‚Äôm trying to say that the food is good, but not great. The presentation, however, is excellent.< /Text>

< Review>
The Service: The staffs are very welcoming. All of them are very professional and efficient, especially my server, David! The general manager, Kevin, definitely has a great team!!

The Food:

Blue Crab Uni Bowl - good to share because you don't want to get full with the rice. It is just the "starter"

Hamo Karaage - thin eel fried with tempura dressing. very crispy and it goes so well with the light dressing.

Sea Bass skewer - Super tender. The sauce is not overly sweet.

Sushi - Super fresh!! The tuna just melted in my mouth. (BTW, the sushi chefs are really Japanese!)

Ginko Nut - my first time trying grilled ginko nuts. Very interesting texture.

Scallop - prepared perfectly! Love the size for appetizer.

They are indeed using great ingredients!

Can't end the meal without something sweet.

Dried persimmon w/ cream cheese, Macha ice-cream & macha cake. My favorite has to be the persimmon!! Great combination with the cream cheese.

The Parking: Valet parking ($10) and Street Metered ($2.5 per hour) 3 hour limit till 9pm.< /Review>

<review>1/31/15

I saw a woman walking through the Ferry Building with a plate of cheesy yum and I demanded she tell me where it came from. She complied and pointed me in the direction of Cowgirl Creamery. We began to walk through the store, and then spotted "the Sidekick" next door.

A man with a really big ball of cheese and a large unit for heating it stood out front of Sidekick. It was kind of unclear how to obtain a plate, but I eventually figured out there were two places to order and pay, one on either side of the man. It was a short wait for the food after we ordered. My husband and I each had the melted asiago cheese on bread. ("Weekend Raclette - $5.95)

The cheese was wonderful, the bread was kind of soggy. It was really messy and hard to eat, but it was good. A few pickled veggies were served on the side.

I'd probably try something else next time we came, but it wasn't disappointing</review>< Rate>

<time>1368493019224<//time><pics>None</pics>< Text>
The sidekick is a mini storefront that deals mainly in milk based beverages and some serious grilled cheese sandwiches. The beverages are quite tasty, and I tried a few of them, which included the raspberry spritzer thing, a cafe au lait, and one of the chocolate based bevs. All of them were fantastic. The sandwiches were good, buttered grilled bread with fantastic cheese and some meat inside. More of a quality over quantity when it comes to the filling, I had no complaints wolfing them down as the denizens of the Ferry Building's shopping habit swarmed around us.
The staff was just super friendly, which isn't uncommon in San Francisco, but it was absolutely pleasant having them be a part of my experience here.< /Text>

<review>The cheese grits with a poached egg and pancetta might not be to everyone's tastes (as a Canuck, it's not something I see very often) but it grew on me. I think they use a sharp cheddar, which gives the grits good flavour, and the egg was poached perfectly.

I've also enjoyed their burrata salad at lunch; there's a healthy dose of burrata, which plays well with the salad's asparagus and green beans. Whether you're grabbing something en route to a ferry, or want to people watch in the busy corridors of the Ferry Building, this is a good place to do so.</review>< user>

<Review>The cafe-style extension of local Cowgirl Creamery, known as Sidekick Cafe & Milk Bar, is situated prominently on the corner adjacent to the Creamery's Ferry Building cheese shop, in the center of the promenade, and serves fresh milk, several varieties of cheeses  to suit anyone's tastes, and all manner of other dairy-based treats.  The grilled cheese with pancetta is strongly suggested, offering all of the intense saltiness of Italian bacon paired with the creaminess that comes with a locally-sourced, fresh cheese of your selection, grilled and melted to perfection.

Other dairy products include a rich, creamy, decadent chocolate mousse and an Earl Grey Tea panna cotta that any desert-lover would enjoy.  If you want fresh, wholesome, locally-sourced ingredients, prepared with comfort food in mind, you've found another great place in San Francisco...< /Review><pics>None<//pics>< Resp>

<rate>4</rate>< review>
Sure, there are probably a lot of options in San Francisco if you want a grilled cheese, but not many of them are as memorable as the Sidekick Cafe & Milk Bar. Located in the Ferry Building and next door to Cowgirl Creamery, the sandwich artisans whip up some pretty delectable dairy products for the famished passerby. Our group munched on the grilled cheese special of the day with goat gouda (um, yes!), gruyere and fromage blanc. I tried it with and without Pancetta and both were gooey with crisp bread and a sweet and spicy relish of some kind that really made the sandwich. My chai milk tea wasn't huge on the flavor, but the friendly service was a huge win. We ended our dairy feast with some chocolate panna cotta. Holy goodness was that little snack a good one! Rich and thick with a smooth and creamy texture, don't miss this little hidden treat on your next visit.<//review>

<rate>1</rate>< text>
Geico sent me to Caliber Collision after some kid hit the front of my Nissan Armada. The car had front end damage, bumper, wheel, and frame.  I sent the car here because of the "lifetime guarantee" and being Geico's preferred shop I figured this was going to be an easy deal. What a mistake I made bringing the car here.

First off when I got the car back, I immediately noticed three major problems.  The repair monkey did not even bolt the bumper to the frame of the vehicle.  There are two large bolts to hold this in and one was missing after repair. I pointed this out to the tech and he scratched his head and said, "...hmm yeah I see that."  Then the wheel well plastic liner separating the tire from the car was completely broken and they did not fix this either.  I again pointed this out. The tech said, "...yeah I see where it is broken.". With the wheels straight you can tell the steering wheel is 30 degrees off. Obviously they didn't do any alignment after the job. The manager came out and told me he would talk to the quality control tech. I highly doubt there is one, if so it has to be a monkey in overalls, he may or may not have a wrench.

After this, I took the car to a competitor of these guys in Chula Vista to have the work verified. Immediately the other shop noticed three more problems I did not and pointed them out in about five seconds.  The fender was never fixed, there are cracks where they attempted to pull it straight I was told. They did not paint or repair another section, and the entire bumper was not set correctly and was off by about an inch. After removing the bumper I was shown more problems, pieces that were cracked and not repaired, as well as the shoddy workmanship of the mounting.

I notified Geico about what has happened. Geico has told Caliber to pay the other auto body company for the repairs. I made sure to document as much as possible. They also took lots of pictures.

I would never take a vehicle to these guys if you want it fixed properly. These guys are absolute knuckleheads at best. I do not understand how they are in business with Geico. I would bet that the happy people writing reviews know absolutely nothing about the quality of their work and I also bet that if these people had a professional look at their work it would be a different story. I believe they have a deal with Geico to fix their cars as fast and as cheap as possible so that they push customers through without having to really repair vehicles correctly.

I also understand why they will not let you take your car without signing their release form in which you agree to binding arbitration in the event you have a dispute with them. This way when you find out how bad their work is you cannot sue them in court.  Lucky for me I can still file a lawsuit against Geico.

Bottom line is if you want to avoid having a major problem take your car elsewhere, their "lifetime guarantee" doesn't matter if your car is not repaired properly in the first place.  I would not listen to Geico either if they try and send you here. Good luck do your research first.</text>

<user_id>116962310690013134908</user_id><date>1562161500750< /date><rating>3<//rating></record></dataset><record>
< review>
My wife and I eat at the food truck in the parking lot.

Really good Mexican food.  The pork is shredded but has a solid flavour.  Would like to highlight that the meat is not watery tasting like other places.  The beef is super cooked but still palatable.  We have tried taccs, super tacos, burritos, and tortas.

The food can be spicy or extra spicy - depending on what you would like.

They also have a restaurant next door that I have eaten at a number of times - similar taste.

It can be busy at times - normally lunch on week days is busy for the restaurant and the truck seems to be quite busy on Saturdays/Sundays around lunch.< /review>

< text>
Open only from 11:30AM to ~2:15PM M-F.  Their trucks outside, and at ~Elco&Lawrence, do not make the very good Wet Burrito Carne Asada, and it is just "Not" the same as inside.  However, inside, The Wet Burrito, is worth walking there barefoot in Summer, to just taste it!  .  .
OMG!  So tasty good, with its Secret  bouquet of Chili Flavor and Zing!  Be sure to ask for Green Salsa too, and that Wet Burrito will do what it says ;-)
I pitty the poor people that do not tip 20% here.  That means bring $12 each with water only.  You will be so satisfied.  Take a second to go for a friend!  They will be so grateful!
Super gorgeous servers, and Cooks who can cook too!
I've never had a Margarita for Lunch in my life before, but I hear they are available.  Exotic bottled beers too.</text>
